registration follows a structured pattern distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime. Controllers in kubernetes/kubernetes are registered and managed through a manager pattern that uses shared informer factories and a controller context.\\n\\n## Key Registration Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface Definition\\nThe base `Interface` type is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`. This interface defines the minimal contract for a controller with a `Name()` method. Controllers can optionally implement the `Debuggable` interface (providing debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (providing health checks).\\n\\n### 2. Controller Manager Context\\nThe `ControllerContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go` acts as the manager, providing:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: for sharing informers across controllers\\n- `ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory`: for generic controller access\\n- `RESTMapper`: for REST resource mapping\\n- `Stop` channel: for graceful shutdown\\n- `InformersStarted` signal: for controller synchronization\\n\\n### 3. Reconciler Patterns\\nMultiple reconciler implementations demonstrate the reconciliation loop pattern:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/reconciler/reconciler.go` defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Run()` method\\n- `pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/reconciler/reconciler.go` implements reconciliation for volume attach/detach\\n- `pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go` defines `EndpointReconciler` for managing API server endpoints\\n\\nThese reconcilers run periodic loops that reconcile desired state with actual state.\\n\\n### 4. Sample Controller Registration Flow\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/` demonstrates the standard pattern:\\n\\n**Initialization** (`main.go`):\\n1. Create informer factories: `kubeinformers.NewSharedInformerFactory()` and custom informer factories\\n2. Create the controller: `NewController(ctx, kubeClient, exampleClient, informers...)`\\n3. Run the controller: `controller.Run(ctx, workerCount)`\\n\\n**Controller Structure** (`controller.go`):\\n- `NewController()` initializes the Controller struct with clients, listers, and work queue\\n- Sets up event handlers on informers to queue work items when resources change\\n- `Run()` method waits for cache sync, then starts worker goroutines\\n- `syncHandler()` is the main reconciliation method that compares desired vs actual state\\n\\n### 5. Main Controller Manager\\nThe `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` file implements the main entry point that:\\n1. Creates a `ControllerContext` with shared informers and clients\\n2. Orchestrates starting multiple controllers in the manager\\n3. Uses `leader election` for HA setups\\n4. Manages the lifecycle of all controllers through the main `Run()` function\\n\\n## Registration Summary\\n\\nUnlike sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime which uses a `SetupWithManager()` pattern, Kubernetes controllers register themselves by:\\n1. Implementing the `Interface` interface with a `Name()` method\\n2. Accepting a `ControllerContext` containing shared resources (informers, clients)\\n3. Implementing a `Run(ctx context.Context, ...)` method that starts the reconciliation loop\\n4. Setting up event handlers on informers to populate a work queue\\n5. Processing items from the work queue in worker goroutines, calling the sync handler\\n\\nThe manager (embodied by the controller manager process and the ControllerContext) is responsible for:\\n- Creating and configuring shared informer factories\\n- Providing clients and REST mappers to controllers\\n- Coordinating informer startup and controller initialization\\n- Managing graceful shutdown through context cancellation\\n- Handling leader election for HA deployments\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":3072,"cache_read_input_tokens":90903,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":3072},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"dd8a8f0c-4e7f-440f-8bd9-cfd6dd4e7a81","uuid":"e365414b-2f90-42fa-bda3-b728d7a746f7"}

registration follows a structured pattern distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime. Controllers in kubernetes/kubernetes are registered and managed through a manager pattern that uses shared informer factories and a controller context.\\n\\n## Key Registration Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface Definition\\nThe base `Interface` type is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`. This interface defines the minimal contract for a controller with a `Name()` method. Controllers can optionally implement the `Debuggable` interface (providing debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (providing health checks).\\n\\n### 2. Controller Manager Context\\nThe `ControllerContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go` acts as the manager, providing:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: for sharing informers across controllers\\n- `ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory`: for generic controller access\\n- `RESTMapper`: for REST resource mapping\\n- `Stop` channel: for graceful shutdown\\n- `InformersStarted` signal: for controller synchronization\\n\\n### 3. Reconciler Patterns\\nMultiple reconciler implementations demonstrate the reconciliation loop pattern:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/reconciler/reconciler.go` defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Run()` method\\n- `pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/reconciler/reconciler.go` implements reconciliation for volume attach/detach\\n- `pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go` defines `EndpointReconciler` for managing API server endpoints\\n\\nThese reconcilers run periodic loops that reconcile desired state with actual state.\\n\\n### 4. Sample Controller Registration Flow\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/` demonstrates the standard pattern:\\n\\n**Initialization** (`main.go`):\\n1. Create informer factories: `kubeinformers.NewSharedInformerFactory()` and custom informer factories\\n2. Create the controller: `NewController(ctx, kubeClient, exampleClient, informers...)`\\n3. Start informer factories: `kubeInformerFactory.Start(ctx.Done())`\\n4. Run the controller: `controller.Run(ctx, workerCount)`\\n\\n**Controller Structure** (`controller.go`):\\n- `NewController()` initializes the Controller struct with clients, listers, and work queue\\n- Sets up event handlers on informers to queue work items when resources change\\n- `Run()` method waits for cache sync, then starts worker goroutines\\n- `syncHandler()` is the main reconciliation method that compares desired vs actual state\\n\\n### 5. Creates a `ControllerContext` with shared informers and clients\\n2. Orchestrates starting multiple controllers in the manager\\n3. Uses `leader election` for HA setups\\n4. Manages the lifecycle of all controllers through the main `Run()` function\\n\\n## Registration Summary\\n\\nUnlike sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime which uses a `SetupWithManager()` pattern, Kubernetes controllers register themselves by:\\n1. registration follows a structured pattern distinct from sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime. Controllers in kubernetes/kubernetes are registered and managed through a manager pattern that uses shared informer factories and a controller context.\\n\\n## Key Registration Components\\n\\n### 1. Controller Interface Definition\\nThe base `Interface` type is defined in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/controller/interfaces.go`. This interface defines the minimal contract for a controller with a `Name()` method. Controllers can optionally implement the `Debuggable` interface (providing debugging handlers) and `HealthCheckable` interface (providing health checks).\\n\\n### 2. Controller Manager Context\\nThe `ControllerContext` in `staging/src/k8s.io/controller-manager/app/controllercontext.go` acts as the manager, providing:\\n- `ClientBuilder`: for creating Kubernetes API clients\\n- `InformerFactory`: for sharing informers across controllers\\n- `ObjectOrMetadataInformerFactory`: for generic controller access\\n- `RESTMapper`: for REST resource mapping\\n- `Stop` channel: for graceful shutdown\\n- `InformersStarted` signal: for controller synchronization\\n\\n### 3. Reconciler Patterns\\nMultiple reconciler implementations demonstrate the reconciliation loop pattern:\\n- `pkg/kubelet/pluginmanager/reconciler/reconciler.go` defines a `Reconciler` interface with a `Run()` method\\n- `pkg/controller/volume/attachdetach/reconciler/reconciler.go` implements reconciliation for volume attach/detach\\n- `pkg/controlplane/reconcilers/reconcilers.go` defines `EndpointReconciler` for managing API server endpoints\\n\\nThese reconcilers run periodic loops that reconcile desired state with actual state.\\n\\n### 4. Sample Controller Registration Flow\\nThe `staging/src/k8s.io/sample-controller/` demonstrates the standard pattern:\\n\\n**Initialization** (`main.go`):\\n1. Create informer factories: `kubeinformers.NewSharedInformerFactory()` and custom informer factories\\n2. Create the controller: `NewController(ctx, kubeClient, exampleClient, informers...)`\\n3. Start informer factories: `kubeInformerFactory.Start(ctx.Done())`\\n4. Run the controller: `controller.Run(ctx, workerCount)`\\n\\n**Controller Structure** (`controller.go`):\\n- `NewController()` initializes the Controller struct with clients, listers, and work queue\\n- Sets up event handlers on informers to queue work items when resources change\\n- `Run()` method waits for cache sync, then starts worker goroutines\\n- `syncHandler()` is the main reconciliation method that compares desired vs actual state\\n\\n### 5. Main Controller Manager\\nThe `cmd/kube-controller-manager/app/controllermanager.go` file implements the main entry point that:\\n1. Creates a `ControllerContext` with shared informers and clients\\n2. Orchestrates starting multiple controllers in the manager\\n3. Uses `leader election` for HA setups\\n4. Manages the lifecycle of all controllers through the main `Run()` function\\n\\n## Registration Summary\\n\\nUnlike sigs.k8s.io/controller-runtime which uses a `SetupWithManager()` pattern, Kubernetes controllers register themselves by:\\n1. Implementing the `Interface` interface with a `Name()` method\\n2. Accepting a `ControllerContext` containing shared resources (informers, clients)\\n3. Implementing a `Run(ctx context.Context, ...)` method that starts the reconciliation loop\\n4. Setting up event handlers on informers to populate a work queue\\n5. Processing items from the work queue in worker goroutines, calling the sync handler\\n\\nThe manager (embodied by the controller manager process and the ControllerContext) is responsible for:\\n- Creating and configuring shared informer factories\\n- Providing clients and REST mappers to controllers\\n- Coordinating informer startup and controller initialization\\n- Managing graceful shutdown through context cancellation\\n- Handling leader election for HA deployments\"\n}\n","numLines":140,"startLine":1,"totalLines":140}}}
